      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17609918240545278741">Long considered the pioneer of the modern Regency genre, Georgette Heyer is legendary among romance readers. This is her charming story of Cleone Charteris, an English belle who yearns for a refined, aristocratic husband...everything Philip Jettan is not! But Philip is determined to convince Cleone that he is the man for her.</span>

            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_218366149">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218366149" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2411388-hannah" class="left imgcol" title="Hannah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1272561978p2/2411388.jpg" alt="Hannah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/218366149?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 05, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2411388-hannah" class="user" title="Hannah">Hannah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6738747-powder-and-patch" title="Paperback 9781402219498" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2411388-hannah?shelf=romances" class="actionLinkLite">romances</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2411388-hannah?shelf=2011-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2011-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer218366149">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12846985520997350974">Totally silly.<br /><br />If it weren't for the fact that this book clocks in at only 183 pages, I would have consigned this to the "did-not-finish" shelf. However, by the time I got fed up enough with it to actually stop reading, it lacked only a few chapters to finish, so WTH.<br /><br />I suppose having a good majority of the book in French might possibly have something to do with my dislike of the novel. Don't get me wrong - French is a beautiful language, and long, long ago I even took it in high school. But for t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12846985520997350974">Totally silly.<br /><br />If it weren't for the fact that this book clocks in at only 183 pages, I would have consigned this to the "did-not-finish" shelf. However, by the time I got fed up enough with it to actually stop reading, it lacked only a few chapters to finish, so WTH.<br /><br />I suppose having a good majority of the book in French might possibly have something to do with my dislike of the novel. Don't get me wrong - French is a beautiful language, and long, long ago I even took it in high school. But for the life of me only a few words remain in my vocabulary (and memory), so to have a book dedicate long passages in French (without translation) was frustrating to say the least. Only imagine having to read my review as follows:<br /><br /><em>Wgent ghth wvlt caqtth, hkqpb ntjfth yhh vdeeo ov vqpp msa fhklhlqq! Agkdhs ghw yww bnhwr't smsqbg yf bbw mvw wovvoa</em>.<br /><br />You get the idea.<br /><br />Another thing that really irritated me was the plot of the story -- a sex reversal of "Cinderella" -- in which our young hero Phillip is dissed by his father and the love of his life, Cleone, for being too...masculine. You see, Cleone doesn't want a manly man. She wants an effeminate fop for her lover, so Phillip decides that instead of telling this little snit of a girl to take him or leave him, he gets all upset that he's not girly enough for his, er, girl, and flounces off to Paris to transform himself into the epitome of mid-18th century couture. (I give to you exhibit A, the "Fop"):<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/photos/1317655889p8/350777.jpg" /><br />I mean, <em>
  <strong>REALLY</strong>
</em>? Does this....thing...make the ovaries tingle in any appreciable way? Well, we come to find out that Cleone isn't too jazzed by the new and improved Phillip either (that's <em>Phillipe</em> to those of you in France). In fact, Cleone is so upset that Phillip/Phillipe has actually done as she wanted, that she spurns his attentions and generally acts like a 5 year old drama queen for the rest of the story.<br /><br /><br />But before you accuse me of just not "digging" the overly-bedazzled, overly-dressed, and overly-fashioned-accessoried man of the past, I present to you exhibit B (well, hello, Callum Blue):<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/photos/1317656378p8/350782.jpg" /><br /><br />OK, so this picture really has nothing germane to add to my review, but I had to slip it in because....well, because this makes <u>my</u> ovaries tingle, if you must know.<br />Anyway, your <em>Showtime</em>-enhanced Tudor-era man knew how to stay manly even with all those velvets and jewels and lace (as well as <em>Showtime</em> leather).<br /><br />But I digress.<br /><br />Anyway, this particular Heyer just didn't work for me this time around. It was way too silly and incomprehensible for my taste.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12846985520997350974">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_83679651">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83679651" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2628389-lucy" class="left imgcol" title="Lucy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1332772679p2/2628389.jpg" alt="Lucy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/83679651?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 17, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2628389-lucy" class="user" title="Lucy">Lucy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311229.Powder_And_Patch" title="Paperback 9780099474432" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer83679651">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7556563240771449279">I’ve only begun reading Heyer’s books as of late last year and can honestly say that so far every single one has been a source of pure delight. No surprise- Powder and Patch followed suit in keeping me well entertained. This book, sweet, short, hilarious, with its oh-so-French flair was completed in one sitting.<br /><br />The book is about Philip Jettan, son to the extravagant Maurice and nephew of Tom. The latter are both highly fashionable men, who are well known in high society; whereas the good-natured</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7556563240771449279">I’ve only begun reading Heyer’s books as of late last year and can honestly say that so far every single one has been a source of pure delight. No surprise- Powder and Patch followed suit in keeping me well entertained. This book, sweet, short, hilarious, with its oh-so-French flair was completed in one sitting.<br /><br />The book is about Philip Jettan, son to the extravagant Maurice and nephew of Tom. The latter are both highly fashionable men, who are well known in high society; whereas the good-natured, but somewhat simpleton and rough-on-the-edges Philip, leaves much to be desired.<br />Philip is, however, the loving flame of Cleone, a neighborhood friend and great beauty. Cleone, along with the rest of Philip’s small family, all agree that the young man should get a make-over to improve his style, fashion sense, etiquette and social skills. Philip is not too keen on this and believes he should be loved for who he is. He makes a strong point- Except that things change dramatically when a certain Bancroft comes to town…<br /><br />Bankroft is handsome, well-mannered, sophisticated, well-versed, and ever so fashionable. He also has a way with the ladies, and Cleone notices him immediately. She is seemingly swooned by Bancroft who pays gracious attention to her every need. Philip notices this but believes that Cleone is his sweetheart and that no one can ever come between them. Cleone admits that she loves Philip but will not take him as he is…he definitely needs refining. She would love him to be more romantic and worldly.<br /><br />The decision is taken by both father and uncle- Philip is to go to France to become more civilized and worldly. Philip, enflamed by jealousy, finally agrees, and off he goes to Paris. There, a huge transformation takes place. Elegance to the max, Philip is the center of all attention- no party is worth going if he’s not present. He’s got style, class, fashion…and, a way with words that makes every woman want to be with him.<br /><br />When he comes back to England, he is a changed man. But Philip wants to know if Cleone really loves the man, or the powder. It is a struggle of wits, suitors for Cleone, love games, jealous rants and more. Cleone is not used to this man who is no longer simple…intriguing to the max, she cannot resist him, yet she will not succumb. What will happen? Do they end up together or will Cleone marry another?<br /><br />I loved this sweet story filled with old French sayings that I hadn’t heard in years (Salipopette!) the details in fashion and Phillip’s mundane experiences were totally amusing. The characters are also perfectly suited to the story. Heyer brings in Louis XV, la Pompadour and other figures of the times to further immerse us into a world of glamour, extravagance and fun- all precisely intended to highten Phillips magnificent make-over. <br /><br />The setting, the language, the story; everything about this book makes it an extremely enjoyable read. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7556563240771449279">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1310309468">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1310309468" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/43278962-daniella" class="left imgcol" title="Daniella"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451900205p2/43278962.jpg" alt="Daniella" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1310309468?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 20, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/43278962-daniella" class="user" title="Daniella">Daniella</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8299139-powder-and-patch" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1310309468">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15971828454492604419">This is my first Georgette Heyer and I really regretted that I started with this book. I should have heeded the warnings of my friends about this novel, but I already bought it so I just went ahead and read it.<br /><br />Let's discuss Cleone. I was actually more forgiving of her at the beginning of the book, because to a certain degree, I kind of understood her desire for Philip to be more "polished." I considered it as a product of her society back then. Considering the historical context, I think it was</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15971828454492604419">This is my first Georgette Heyer and I really regretted that I started with this book. I should have heeded the warnings of my friends about this novel, but I already bought it so I just went ahead and read it.<br /><br />Let's discuss Cleone. I was actually more forgiving of her at the beginning of the book, because to a certain degree, I kind of understood her desire for Philip to be more "polished." I considered it as a product of her society back then. Considering the historical context, I think it was natural or normal to put a lot of importance on appearances and whatnot. In that vein, I don't really fault Cleone; it's what she did halfway through the book that annoyed me. When Philip proposed to her a second time, she got angry at him for being a flirt in Paris. Um, hello? Weren't you blatantly flirting with Henry in front of Philip before? Double-standards, much? Ugh. And then she goes on to get engaged with two gentlemen. What the fuck? <br /><br /><img width="400" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434821534ra/15266682.gif" /><br /><br />By the end of the book, Cleone managed to convince me that she's nothing but a stupid, silly, and selfish girl who does not deserve Philip's love.<br /><br />I felt really bad for Philip, James and all of the readers who have to endure Cleone's existence.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15971828454492604419">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_676422">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/676422" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/56479-res" class="left imgcol" title="Res"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1177127447p2/56479.jpg" alt="Res" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/676422?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 11, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/56479-res" class="user" title="Res">Res</a>

        rated it

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/5853766-kelly-instalove" class="user" title="Kelly_Instalove">Kelly_Instalove</a>

          marked it as dnf-dnr


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8299139-powder-and-patch" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5853766-kelly-instalove?shelf=genre-romance" class="actionLinkLite">genre-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5853766-kelly-instalove?shelf=theme-disguise" class="actionLinkLite">theme-disguise</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5853766-kelly-instalove?shelf=era-historical" class="actionLinkLite">era-historical</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer198276004">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6280387847455874336">Chronological order was definitely not the best choice for my 2012 Georgette Heyer Reading Challenge.<br /><br />I made it through <a title="The Black Moth by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322.The_Black_Moth">The Black Moth</a> relatively painlessly, but this one really went downhill halfway through - which, ironically, was the point at which the plot kicked in.<br /><br />While Phillip's dandifying was the premise of the book, the constant and nearly impenetrable Regency slang following his transformation just wasn't worth the effort needed to decipher it.<br /><br />I'm a big proponent of historical accuracy,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6280387847455874336">Chronological order was definitely not the best choice for my 2012 Georgette Heyer Reading Challenge.<br /><br />I made it through <a title="The Black Moth by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322.The_Black_Moth">The Black Moth</a> relatively painlessly, but this one really went downhill halfway through - which, ironically, was the point at which the plot kicked in.<br /><br />While Phillip's dandifying was the premise of the book, the constant and nearly impenetrable Regency slang following his transformation just wasn't worth the effort needed to decipher it.<br /><br />I'm a big proponent of historical accuracy, but Heyer must have confused quantity with quality at this early point in her writing. The use of historic slang was also a big part of <a title="April Lady by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311121.April_Lady">April Lady</a>*, but in the 34 years between the two novels (1923, 1957), Heyer obviously learned to use it much more subtly and effectively.<br /><br />I'm determined to finish the last half of this by the end of the year, but only to say that I've read every Heyer book.<br /><br />----<br /><br /><em>* yeah, I read out of order, my hold at the library came through much earlier than expected, so whatever</em></span>

          </span>

      <a href="/user/show/1024907-terra" class="user" title="Terra">Terra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer84436297">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8788425961439532982">Powder and Patch by Georgette Heyer is an exceptional story of the purity of the Regency period that we love so dearly. If you are a fan of Jane Austen and haven't read Miss Heyer yet then what are you waiting for.<br /><br />Cleone Charteris is a young lady of fine manners and undeniable beauty. As with most young ladies of this time however, she is also a bit of spoiled snob. She is of marriageable age and the young man who would give his life in order to protect hers is much to plain and common in his ap</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8788425961439532982">Powder and Patch by Georgette Heyer is an exceptional story of the purity of the Regency period that we love so dearly. If you are a fan of Jane Austen and haven't read Miss Heyer yet then what are you waiting for.<br /><br />Cleone Charteris is a young lady of fine manners and undeniable beauty. As with most young ladies of this time however, she is also a bit of spoiled snob. She is of marriageable age and the young man who would give his life in order to protect hers is much to plain and common in his appearance for her.<br /><br />Philip Jettan is a hard working man but one without polish. He is strong, honest and so sure that his dear love Cleone will accept him as he is that upon his asking for her hand in marriage he is devastated when she refuses because he is a plain country bumpkin instead of a painted popinjay.<br /><br />Our author writes her stories with a purity of heart and soul that is nothing short of a breath of fresh air. She takes our plain country bumpkin and makes him into a finely polished gem that sparkles brighter than the stars in the heavens. A hero that is much sot after in the world of paint, powder and power that anyone who knew of him before said transition is utterly astonished at the remarkable transformation that has come about so quickly.<br /><br />The hundred dollar question is though, will Philip remember his roots and his love for Cleone after all he has done and gone through? Will the lust of power and the challenge of the game of the upstairs society lure him towards total refinement or will his past have enough of a life line to him to keep him in check with who he truly is under all the Powder and Patch?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8788425961439532982">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6782403720738686571">Powder and Patch isn't set in the Regency period. It's set about 20 years before most of Heyer's other work. The clues to this are subtle, though, and easy to miss--mainly having to do with fashion (men wearing powdered wigs, patches, and lace) and with the nobles Philip meets in France--or, indeed, there being nobles in France.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9283033498794869341">Well written, of coarse it's Georgette Heyer. I strongly disliked Cleone, the love interest of the main character Philip. I found her insipid, stupid, self centered and boring. I hate it when the object of a man's affections has nothing to recommend her except her beauty. Not all women can or should be like Jane Eyre, but they should be something more than just nice to look at, she could at least have been kind.<br />I liked Philip better before he changed, he was much more manly and attractive soundi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9283033498794869341">Well written, of coarse it's Georgette Heyer. I strongly disliked Cleone, the love interest of the main character Philip. I found her insipid, stupid, self centered and boring. I hate it when the object of a man's affections has nothing to recommend her except her beauty. Not all women can or should be like Jane Eyre, but they should be something more than just nice to look at, she could at least have been kind.<br />I liked Philip better before he changed, he was much more manly and attractive sounding. I feel very sorry for women of this time period, it has to have been the most unattractive time for men. Wigs, powder, rouge, tights do not belong on any straight hetero. man. ugh. I will try again with Georgette Heyer, maybe the next one will have more likable characters.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer110014796">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer589491588856801954">This book was better than Georgette Heyer's first book The Black Moth. In here, she does concentrate on both the heroine and the hero. Phillip Jettan prefers the backwater of his life. He is also enamored of a neighbor's daughter, Cleon Charteris. Then Cleon meets man about town, Sir Henry Bancroft. Now Phillip looks uncouth to her. She demands he learns the correct manner of address and dressing. Hurt, after a mock duel in which he is bested, Phillip retreats to Paris. Meeting Cleon some times</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText589491588856801954">This book was better than Georgette Heyer's first book The Black Moth. In here, she does concentrate on both the heroine and the hero. Phillip Jettan prefers the backwater of his life. He is also enamored of a neighbor's daughter, Cleon Charteris. Then Cleon meets man about town, Sir Henry Bancroft. Now Phillip looks uncouth to her. She demands he learns the correct manner of address and dressing. Hurt, after a mock duel in which he is bested, Phillip retreats to Paris. Meeting Cleon some times later with him painted and patched, she barely recognizes him. Now she is not so sure she likes this new version.<br />Cleone is not so perfect herself and gets herself into a fine compromising situation! <br />This is a quick, easy fun read. Very enjoyable.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="589491588856801954">...more</a>

        <a href="/review/show/143454440?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 25, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart" class="user" title="Jane Stewart">Jane Stewart</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/9836305-powder-and-patch" title="MP3 Book 9781408436295" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer143454440">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15193517311564375723">A farce trying to be humorous but it wasn’t. I was not entertained.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />Phillip is happy with his simple life as a country farmer. He doesn’t wear fine clothes. He has no desire for the social life. Phillip and Cleone love each other. Henry comes to town and flirts with Cleone. Cleone is impressed that Henry is well dressed. Cleone tells Phillip she wants him to gain polish and to dress better. Phillip goes to Paris to transform himself. He learns French and how to fence, dress, and be en</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15193517311564375723">A farce trying to be humorous but it wasn’t. I was not entertained.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />Phillip is happy with his simple life as a country farmer. He doesn’t wear fine clothes. He has no desire for the social life. Phillip and Cleone love each other. Henry comes to town and flirts with Cleone. Cleone is impressed that Henry is well dressed. Cleone tells Phillip she wants him to gain polish and to dress better. Phillip goes to Paris to transform himself. He learns French and how to fence, dress, and be entertaining. He wears wigs, powder, rouge, and jewels. When he sees Cleone again, she believes untrue gossip about him which causes problems.<br /><br />REVIEWER’S OPINION:<br />There were many French phrases, and I did not understand any of them. I guess that was ok, since most of that conversation was silly and meant to be like party chit- chat. When Phillip goes to Paris we don’t see the transformation process which I would have liked. Instead we are quickly taken to six months later where he is an excellent swordsman and fun party-goer. When he returns to England, the plot with Cleone was farcical. Conflicts were based on silly misunderstandings with neither party communicating in a reasonable manner. For example, he loves her but he acts like he doesn’t – because he wants to test her or teach her a lesson.<br /><br />Cleone was finicky, scatterbrained, stupid, shallow, and irritating. The intent was humor, but I didn’t find it funny. There was also an odd issue. Apparently Cleone could believe two opposing ideas and wanted Phillip to “master her” into the right decisions. Apparently she had no logic or decision making ability.<br /><br />This was one of Heyer’s early works. It’s about half the length of most of her books. I consider it an experiment on her part and not worth buying unless you are a rabid Heyer fan and want to read everything she does. The narrator was fine. I enjoyed hearing him speak the French phrases.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Unabridged audiobook length: 5 hours 5 minutes. Narrator: Jamie Glover. Swearing language: none. Sexual content: none. Setting: 1753 Paris, France, Little Fittledean and London, England. Copyright: 1930. Genre: historical romance.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1735047576049353159">Everytime I read a Georgette Heyer novel I think its my favorite so far as I do with this one. If you haven't read a Heyer novel start off with this one as its shorter (about 200 pages) than her others novels and gets straight into the love conflict early on (not as slow as her other novels). Cleone is a beautiful country woman who has an admirer Philip Jettan but he has not toured Europe or become a Gentleman as per her standards. He does not like to be a painted puppet as he put it. When Cleon</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1735047576049353159">Everytime I read a Georgette Heyer novel I think its my favorite so far as I do with this one. If you haven't read a Heyer novel start off with this one as its shorter (about 200 pages) than her others novels and gets straight into the love conflict early on (not as slow as her other novels). Cleone is a beautiful country woman who has an admirer Philip Jettan but he has not toured Europe or become a Gentleman as per her standards. He does not like to be a painted puppet as he put it. When Cleone makes it very clear that she can't marry a man who isn't, Philip is finally motivated to listen to his fathers encouragement to go stay with his uncle in London and learn how to become a Gentlemen. His uncle sends him to Paris where he is refined and becomes quite the thing (even learns how to use his sword which will be needed more than once for a duel over a woman) with loads of charm, friends and French lingo in each sentence. When Cleone sees the real Philip she wants the old Philip back but he doesn't realize that. What a fun read! Of course you know they'll end up together but the journey to that point gets quite hilarious! If I had to give it a 4.5 stars instead of 5 it would be due to the French lines and poems I didn't understand since I don't know any French.. otherwise its a 5 for me!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer241369682">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7974270768251694729">Powder and Patch is a lighter piece of fluff for Georgette Heyer, and much shorter in length than the majority of her novels. The book centralizes on two characters, Philip and Cleone. Here is the synopsis:<br /><br />The charm of Powder and Patch, as with many of Heyer's other novels, is her discourse on the social customs of the time, revealed through character exchanges and descriptions of dress and mannerisms for both ladies and gentleman. There is certainly a lot of great description of the clothing an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7974270768251694729">Powder and Patch is a lighter piece of fluff for Georgette Heyer, and much shorter in length than the majority of her novels. The book centralizes on two characters, Philip and Cleone. Here is the synopsis:<br /><br />The charm of Powder and Patch, as with many of Heyer's other novels, is her discourse on the social customs of the time, revealed through character exchanges and descriptions of dress and mannerisms for both ladies and gentleman. There is certainly a lot of great description of the clothing and accoutrement from the Georgian period in Power and Patch. Of course, what constitutes a gentleman has changed from era to era, in the Georgian period gentlemen must have great "love making" technique, have a certain air and posture, be a wonderful dancer, have a sly wit and, of course, must have great swordsmanship for all those duels to defend "my lady's" honour. Anyhoo, Powder and Patch is a fun read. I highly recommend for fans of Georgette Heyer but would recommend The Grand Sophy, The Nonesuch or Arabella instead for Heyer first timers. <br /><br />My Rating: 3.5<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://myobsessionwithbooks.blogspot.com/" target="_blank">http://myobsessionwithbooks.blogspot....</a></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_240364469">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240364469" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4181111-kathryn" class="left imgcol" title="Kathryn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1320032014p2/4181111.jpg" alt="Kathryn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/240364469?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 27, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4181111-kathryn" class="user" title="Kathryn">Kathryn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6738747-powder-and-patch" title="Paperback 9781402219498" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4181111-kathryn?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer240364469">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8617217581322647865"><em>Powder and Patch</em> is an interesting change from Heyer's other books, and unfortunately, the change isn't entirely positive. Philip Jettan, the main character, is in love with a girl named Cleone, but she tells him she doesn't want him until he learns a bit more address; Philip disdains the frippery of the fashionable world. After a young man who does have the address Philip lacks pays court to Cleone, Philip hies himself to France to learn how to be a fashionable gentleman. He succeeds and eventu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8617217581322647865"><em>Powder and Patch</em> is an interesting change from Heyer's other books, and unfortunately, the change isn't entirely positive. Philip Jettan, the main character, is in love with a girl named Cleone, but she tells him she doesn't want him until he learns a bit more address; Philip disdains the frippery of the fashionable world. After a young man who does have the address Philip lacks pays court to Cleone, Philip hies himself to France to learn how to be a fashionable gentleman. He succeeds and eventually wins Cleone's heart.<br /><br />This is a book where Heyer's rather sexist notions about romance really come to the forefront. I'm most fond of her older heroine novels, such as <em>Black Sheep</em>, precisely because they tend to deviate from those ideas, but even in those cases, the declaration of love almost always seems to require that a previously strong woman bend to a stronger male character. I can usually gloss over that bit, but in <em>Powder and Patch</em>, almost the entire last third of the book involves characters discoursing on how foolish women are and how Philip should use anything <em>but</em> frankness and reason to attempt to gain Cleone's hand in marriage. Granted, Cleone <em>is</em> pretty foolish, but who's to blame for that but the author?<br /><br />I just can't really connect with the characters. I like Philip <em>before</em> he gains his town-bronze, but not very much after, and I don't like Cleone much at any point of the story. So it's pretty hard to enjoy this book.<br /><br />(The large sections of untranslated French are also pretty annoying.)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8617217581322647865">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1411123187">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4637875689713807945">I think the saving grace for this book was that it was a short read. Once again I am addicted to the over the top, melodramatic language of the era and the pleasure it brings me is why I will always come back to the genre! It is what I enjoyed here as well. However, there was something missing from the story, albeit it was better than the first book, The Black Moth. This is the second book by this author and it shows signs of her greatness to come...</span>

      <a href="/user/show/700357-ladiibbug" class="user" title="Ladiibbug">Ladiibbug</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1212352323">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15033427959748820140">Historical Romance<br /><br />Georgette Heyer for me is always a delightful read. Originally published in 1923, this still stands today as a fun book.<br /><br />Phillip is a quiet young man, a "country squire". He is madly in love with a girl in the village, Cleone. Cleone likes Phillip, but wishes Phillip had travelled, wore more stylish clothes, and was a more exciting personality.<br /><br />Phillip travels to Paris and London in order to learn how to be the kind of personality Cleone desires. He quickly picks up the art of we</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15033427959748820140">Historical Romance<br /><br />Georgette Heyer for me is always a delightful read. Originally published in 1923, this still stands today as a fun book.<br /><br />Phillip is a quiet young man, a "country squire". He is madly in love with a girl in the village, Cleone. Cleone likes Phillip, but wishes Phillip had travelled, wore more stylish clothes, and was a more exciting personality.<br /><br />Phillip travels to Paris and London in order to learn how to be the kind of personality Cleone desires. He quickly picks up the art of wearing the latest over-the-top fashions of that era. He immerses himself in Paris society. He learns enough French phrases to send witty poems to delight and charm young ladies, learns how to use powder, rouge and other cosmetics men of society wear to go with their colorful peacock-like clothing.<br /><br />When Phillip and Cleone meet again, he has become so much the darling of the ladies in Paris that Cleone is jealous. They play the little games of that era until they find their HEA.<br /><br />There was only one date in the book, so it's hard to say, but this was set in the early 1700's I think. I did not know men of any era used rouge, face powder or cosmetics!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1196420533">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1196420533" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6945307-damaskcat" class="left imgcol" title="Damaskcat"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1395844674p2/6945307.jpg" alt="Damaskcat" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1196420533?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 12, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6945307-damaskcat" class="user" title="Damaskcat">Damaskcat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13020996-powder-and-patch" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1196420533">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17192944139012631205">Philip Jettan is in love with Cleone Charteris the daughter of one of his neighbours. But Cleone does not appreciate Philip's good qualities - his reliability, sobriety and steadfastness. She yearns for someone a little more polished with society manners and fancy clothes. Philip's father, Sir Maurice, would like to see his son become a man of the world. Between them they persuade Philip to go to London to visit his Uncle Tom who is very much a man about town. Tom vows to transform his dowdy nep</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17192944139012631205">Philip Jettan is in love with Cleone Charteris the daughter of one of his neighbours. But Cleone does not appreciate Philip's good qualities - his reliability, sobriety and steadfastness. She yearns for someone a little more polished with society manners and fancy clothes. Philip's father, Sir Maurice, would like to see his son become a man of the world. Between them they persuade Philip to go to London to visit his Uncle Tom who is very much a man about town. Tom vows to transform his dowdy nephew and takes him to Paris so that he can learn to be a well dressed gentleman.<br /><br />The transformation is well done and amusing as it shows how Philip resists his mentors but then throws himself whole heartedly into the process. After 6 months he returns to England apparently and outwardly changed. The dialogue is amusing and the characters well drawn and believable. Cleone is perhaps one of the silliest of Heyer's heroines but she is still delightful. The book's main character is the charming Philip with his ability to laugh at himself and at the follies of the world.<br /><br />This novel is one of my favourites for its sheer light heartedness. None of the characters are wholly bad or wholly good and people change over the course of the story. There are deeper themes about outward appearances and inward qualities but these are not laboured. If you have not read Heyer before this would be a good novel to start with.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17192944139012631205">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1096021487">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1096021487" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8132351-adam" class="left imgcol" title="Adam"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1331375042p2/8132351.jpg" alt="Adam" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1096021487?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 04, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8132351-adam" class="user" title="Adam">Adam</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311200.Powder_And_Patch" title=" 9780553047325" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8132351-adam?shelf=un-put-down-able" class="actionLinkLite">un-put-down-able</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8132351-adam?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1096021487">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17132307118117839517">This rather ridiculous romantic novel set sometime in the 18th century long before the French Revolution is wonderfully enjoyable. It is a delightful romp from beginning to end.<br /><br />Heyer plunges the reader straight into the 18th century. Without any feeling that the author was writing much more than a century later, the reader feels that he or she is reading something written in the earlier period. Like Peter Carey, Georgette Heyer - at least in this the first of her novels that I have read - writes</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17132307118117839517">This rather ridiculous romantic novel set sometime in the 18th century long before the French Revolution is wonderfully enjoyable. It is a delightful romp from beginning to end.<br /><br />Heyer plunges the reader straight into the 18th century. Without any feeling that the author was writing much more than a century later, the reader feels that he or she is reading something written in the earlier period. Like Peter Carey, Georgette Heyer - at least in this the first of her novels that I have read - writes in a way that does not make me feel as if she is trying to impress me with the historical research that she must have done to produce such a credible work of historical fiction. She and Carey immerse the reader into another era without having to resort to using blunt or crude signposting. As I read this novel, I felt myself being dissolved into another era as effortlessly as sugar dissolves into hot tea. This is historical fiction at its best.<br /><br />Although the plot of this novel is light, it is handled marvellously and most amusingly. If it has not been already made into a movie or a stage play, it ought to be: "Powder and Patch" is 'en effet' a veritable comedy of errors.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17132307118117839517">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4267792641334010490">This was a fast, fun read that sported sword play, swooning and a young woman being chased by several young suitors and being engaged to all of them. I usually don't read romance but this one wasn't so painful as I thought it would be. The writing wasn't exactly my cup of tea but it didn't require much thought, something I think I need now and then between those big novels that I think I need to read!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1173204323?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 10, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5433333-margaret-sullivan" class="user" title="Margaret Sullivan">Margaret Sullivan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5433333-margaret-sullivan?shelf=audiobooks" class="actionLinkLite">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5433333-margaret-sullivan?shelf=all-of-heyer-project" class="actionLinkLite">all-of-heyer-project</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5433333-margaret-sullivan?shelf=2015" class="actionLinkLite">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1173204323">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10253790915894178021"><em>This is a shorter version of a <a rel="nofollow" href="http://habitofjournaling.com/2015/02/10/all-of-heyer-powder-and-patch/">post on my blog</a>.</em><br /><br /><em>Powder and Patch</em> is not one of Heyer’s best-known or best-loved novels, though it’s very entertaining. It also had an interesting journey to publication–both times.<br /><br />The novel begins with the history of the Jettans, bringing us up to about the 1750s and the present squire, the widowed Sir Maurice, who had a misspent youth in London and Paris, but has settled down in the country, raising his son Philip at his estate in Sussex. Philip scorns everything</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10253790915894178021"><em>This is a shorter version of a <a rel="nofollow" href="http://habitofjournaling.com/2015/02/10/all-of-heyer-powder-and-patch/">post on my blog</a>.</em><br /><br /><em>Powder and Patch</em> is not one of Heyer’s best-known or best-loved novels, though it’s very entertaining. It also had an interesting journey to publication–both times.<br /><br />The novel begins with the history of the Jettans, bringing us up to about the 1750s and the present squire, the widowed Sir Maurice, who had a misspent youth in London and Paris, but has settled down in the country, raising his son Philip at his estate in Sussex. Philip scorns everything fashionable, and to his father’s despair, is countrified and bumptious. He falls in love with Cleone Charteris, a neighbor’s daughter, and wishes to marry her. Cleone, however, is not quite ready to settle down, and flirts with a Mr. Bancroft, the son of a another neighbor, who is rusticating after fighting a duel. Mr. Bancroft is all that is fashionable and fabulous; Philip is jealous and challenges Bancroft to a duel. As he has scorned taking fencing lessons, Bancroft pinks him. Philip nonetheless proposes to Cleone, who tells him to come back when he has learned to be a gentleman. Sir Maurice agrees that Philip needs some polish, and sends him off to Paris, where he learns to dress, speak French, fence, and flirt, while never forgetting Cleone. Cleone goes to visit her aunt in London, where she encounters the transformed Philip. He still loves her, but also still wants her to want him for himself, not for his polish.<br /><br />The story is hugely entertaining and very much in the vein of Heyer’s later Georgian-set novels, with the swashbuckling flavor of <em>The Black Moth</em>. However, there were some parts that were a little cringe-inducing for a 21st-century reader. There is one scene late in the book in which Cleone’s aunt is advising Philip in his campaign to win Cleone. She basically says to him that when Cleone says no, she means yes, and he should be “brutal” in overcoming her objections. From a modern perspective, this is troubling, but then my last re-reads of <em>Pride and Prejudice</em> and <em>Mansfield Park</em> left me troubled by all the times Elizabeth Bennet and Fanny Price say “no” and men don’t accept it, so my consciousness has been thoroughly raised, I suppose. One is tempted to chalk this up to clumsiness by a young author–Heyer was still only 20 years old when she wrote this. But Cleone and Philip are rather young and silly and overly dramatic, and the older characters, as well as the narrator, know this and are amused by it, which is remarkable from such a young author, so that’s not an excuse. I think this is just another of those things that we have to chalk up to “things were different back then.” And Cleone really did want Philip to “brutally” overcome her objections–to be “masterful” as Heyer calls it. And maybe those particular word choices and manner of description are both the mark of a youthful author and of a different time.<br /><br />Anyway, the book is a quick and enjoyable read–as Heyer herself called it when inscribing her father’s copy, “an elegant trifle.” <br /><br />As a side note, I listened to <em>Powder and Patch</em> as an audiobook from Audible, read by Jamie Glover. He did an excellent job, particularly with the French (there’s a lot of it) and the French accents of various characters. If you like audiobooks, I recommend it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10253790915894178021">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12210566884714123821">Ok la. <br /><br />So Cleone and Philip like each other but being a girl who is very much engineered to behave as how the society dictates it to be, Cleone resents Philip's lack of air of London Society. Driven by his immense love towards Cleone, Philip took off to Paris and came back polished and powdered, literally. Not to mention with French fluency of flattering adjectives that gets all the girls swooning over him as well. The sight of Philip now is a magical one would seize in memory but he still has h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12210566884714123821">Ok la. <br /><br />So Cleone and Philip like each other but being a girl who is very much engineered to behave as how the society dictates it to be, Cleone resents Philip's lack of air of London Society. Driven by his immense love towards Cleone, Philip took off to Paris and came back polished and powdered, literally. Not to mention with French fluency of flattering adjectives that gets all the girls swooning over him as well. The sight of Philip now is a magical one would seize in memory but he still has his heart only for her (ddaw such a gentleman). The author knows just the right trait to have us girls melted and harbouring the oddest trait in our romantic expectations aite gg. <br /><br />But when he comes back, Cleone now is not sure if she has made a terrible mistake or what. Dun dun dun.<br /><br />Personal reflection; I think, the part that I like about the book is the fact that Philip actually did what he hate the most to please his love. While I might risk myself sounding like a typical girl who only wants to dictate a guy to only follow her lead in the relationship, allow me to argue that what she did was what exactly Philip needed. Philip might hated it, he also always have this idea that he will only do this to prove how wrong Cleone was but it turned out to be that he is very good at it that he was able to master the art of being a gentleman only in six months. Admirable indeed. And above all, I think he was still able to persevere the part of good old Philip as he always has the antithesis to Cleone's expectations. Cleone on the other hand, found that she was baffled by her own expectations. At the sight of the new Philip, contrary to what she has always hoped for, a part of her regrets sending him away to be polished. <br /><br />Sometimes in life, we are too overwhelmed by the notion that, if someone sincerely loves you, he/she would just accept you the way you are right. but I think if you sincerely love someone you would want to see them to reach their maximum potential. If you have to be the devil who nags 24/7 for that to happen so be it. Sometimes think that they are already good as they are. At the comfort of that thought, they tend to dismiss other good qualities. Ya lah, it might need some hard kneading to get that trait built but if you also really love someone, wouldn't you want them to have the best version of you? </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_593665058">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/593665058" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10394610-ceecee" class="left imgcol" title="Ceecee"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1375093396p2/10394610.jpg" alt="Ceecee" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/593665058?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 04, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10394610-ceecee" class="user" title="Ceecee">Ceecee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6738747-powder-and-patch" title="Paperback 9781402219498" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who want to read all GH</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ceecee by: </span>
      i don't need a recommendation. it's a GH romance.
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=2-star" class="actionLinkLite">2-star</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=i-finally-found-you" class="actionLinkLite">i-finally-found-you</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer593665058">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2616384487487228031">I do believe this is the second romance GH wrote? Or at least, it <em>was</em> the second published, with the title "The Transformation of Philip Jettan" under the pseudonym Stella Martin, by Mills and Boon in 1923. When it was republished as Powder and Patch in 1930, they left out the original last chapter, which makes me very curious indeed what that original last chapter was. <strong>Please let me know what was in that chapter if you find it, dear Reader.</strong><br /><br />Anyway, I really don't think this is a strong Georgette</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2616384487487228031">I do believe this is the second romance GH wrote? Or at least, it <em>was</em> the second published, with the title "The Transformation of Philip Jettan" under the pseudonym Stella Martin, by Mills and Boon in 1923. When it was republished as Powder and Patch in 1930, they left out the original last chapter, which makes me very curious indeed what that original last chapter was. <strong>Please let me know what was in that chapter if you find it, dear Reader.</strong><br /><br />Anyway, I really don't think this is a strong Georgette Heyer. There was little, if ever, of the prosy, yet witty, narrations and dialogues I was used to in Heyer's later works. Since this is one of her earlier works, I suppose this is understandable. However, I did see little glimpses of Heyer here that would show in the novels that I would come to love. Most especially: the steadfast and intelligent male protagonist.<br /><br />Here's the deal: Philip and Cleone are in love with each other, but Philip is, as they say, a country bumpkin. Everyone agrees that Philip is a good man, but as he is (he is too arrogant in his ways), he cannot be with Cleone. They think Philip needs to strike the balance between a polished gentleman, and the steadfast and honest man that he thinks he is.<br /><br />After sorely losing in a duel, Philip decides to go to Paris and acquire polish, to show them all. Remarkably, he succeeds, in the space of six months. Which, I have to agree, is really rather unrealistic. How does anyone acquire great sword skills, a great taste for fashion and clothing, and a popular reputation in <em>Paris</em>, all in 6 months? <br /><br />In any case, Philip did. Cleone, in the meantime, regrets having forced Philip to acquire polish, hears the gossip that Philip fought in a duel in Paris for a French lady. She thinks Philip has changed for the worse. There's no use waiting around for him, so off she goes to London to show Philip she can go on without him, as he so obviously did.<br /><br />But really, these two people love each other. Philip just wants to know if Cleone loved him for who he is, or the fop she wants him to be.<br /><br />And then commences a series of misunderstandings, which I think didn't stretch into a melodrama, thank God. Thanks to Wise Elders, and an Intelligent Hero, the misunderstandings were cleared up, and they lived happily ever after.<br /><br />Many dislike Powder and Patch, I've read, because of Cleone, and mayhaps because of her contradictory nature. <strong>For my part, I do sympathize with her.</strong> I suppose any woman would like to change something in the man she loves, but Cleone soon regrets this. She was also hurt because she thinks Philip flirted and even fought duels for other ladies. I was a bit surprised though, that she would accuse Philip of having a tarnished reputation. <br /><br />There was also the instance when Cleone, rejecting Philip, secretly wanted him to master her and overcome her fences. When Philip goes to Cleone's aunt, Lady Malmerstoke, dispenses a bit of eyebrow-raising advise: In a sense: That women do not like gentleness in men, and want them to <em>master</em> women, of all words. <strong>Now, I certainly do not want any man to lord over me! </strong><br /><br />However, Lady Malmerstoke admitted herself that she was not that kind of girl in her younger years, and explained to Philip that <strong>girls are very much capable of holding two contradictory thoughts together.</strong> Which I think was a funny scene and rang true. I suppose that what she meant was, sometimes, women want men to assert themselves. In Powder and Patch's context, Philip was not really that assertive, he just acted like Cleone was his for the taking and therefore did not make much effort to woo her.<br /><br /><strong>*2.5 stars</strong> It was light, funny romance, but I really hate misunderstandings and such. I don't think Powder and Patch was strong. The ending felt a bit of a rush and too neatly tied up, though I was still happy that Philip and Cleone ended up happy together.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2616384487487228031">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681795964" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/22177907-qnpoohbear" class="left imgcol" title="QNPoohBear"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1394921233p2/22177907.jpg" alt="QNPoohBear" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/681795964?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 20, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/22177907-qnpoohbear" class="user" title="QNPoohBear">QNPoohBear</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2994625-powder-and-patch" title="Hardcover " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=clean-romance" class="actionLinkLite">clean-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=georgian-romance" class="actionLinkLite">georgian-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=kisses-only" class="actionLinkLite">kisses-only</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer681795964">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12115524195271161521"> This Georgian era set novel is one of Georgette Heyer's earliest works published as "The Transformation of Philip Jettan" under the pseudonym Stella Martin. I would not have wanted to attach my name to this work either if I were her. This is possibly her worst novel ever. The writing style is simplistic but peppered with mostly unintelligible French phrases. The plot doesn't flow very smoothly. The relationships don't feel natural or even interesting. It's a classic misunderstanding plot that w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12115524195271161521"> This Georgian era set novel is one of Georgette Heyer's earliest works published as "The Transformation of Philip Jettan" under the pseudonym Stella Martin. I would not have wanted to attach my name to this work either if I were her. This is possibly her worst novel ever. The writing style is simplistic but peppered with mostly unintelligible French phrases. The plot doesn't flow very smoothly. The relationships don't feel natural or even interesting. It's a classic misunderstanding plot that works fine in short stories. Most of the novel is dedicated to the transformation of Philip and even that is greatly rushed. The heroine is one of the worst sorts who flirts and gets angry at the man she loves for no good reason. The novel finally concludes with some outdated ideas about male/female power and thought process which I did not like at all! Most of Heyer's other heroines are not so awful. There are also brief appearances by a black page named Sambo (the novel was written around 1930) who utters his lines in appalling dialect. I'm surprised this novel has endured for so long. I would not recommend it. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12115524195271161521">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14715383957700691024">I enjoyed this book which I've read at least 3 times before (1/75 when Leo came to London and 10/89 and 6/92 in CT). it's not as good as some of her others and I quite see that if you're not fluent in French it might be annoying. <span id="freeTextContainer12454430254994234084">The one star reviews make me a little sad, but I tend to understand them. However, while Cleone is certainly not my favourite Heyer heroine, I did enjoy the book for its sweet lightheartedness, and I also developed a little crush on Philip/Philippe. 5 years of school French under my belt came in handy, or my pleasure would have been crucially dimmed, I'm certain. So even if I usually prefer the Regency ones among Heyer's novels, this is definitely among my personal top ten.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9572830626331847412">I had my doubts about this book at first, until I read what it was about. You hear about women becoming Cinderella-ized, but not often men. And the back of the book did not make the heroine seem flattering.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText9572830626331847412">I had my doubts about this book at first, until I read what it was about. You hear about women becoming Cinderella-ized, but not often men. And the back of the book did not make the heroine seem flattering. It is hard to like the hero when he chases after someone unworthy for the length of the book.<br /><br />But it was worth it, for the Cinderella-ized man, and for the woman who was stronger than I thought. In fact, reading through it, it reminds me less of Cinderella and more of the movie Easy A. The transformation of the hero, Jettan, has bite to it. And a great deal of humor. I love the duel and all his odes.<br /><br />Overall, another great work by Georgette Heyer.</span>
